ANNEX | 
DEFINITIONS 


The Group of Experts on Transport Statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the United Nations Economic Commission for Europe has agreed 
to the following definitions for the collection of statistical data included in the Annual Bulletin of Transport Statistics for Europe. These definitions are those 
contained in document TRANS/WP6/54 Rev.4, account being taken of subsequent amendments and additions by the Group of Experts, as well as of new 
definitions necessitated by additions to the questionnaires. Where the secretariat has been made aware that governments have been unable to comply with certain 
of the definitions, any such significant departures are indicated by means of footnotes to the relevant tables. 


ALL MODES OF TRANSPORT 
ik Network: A group of tracks or lines of communication. This term is defined below for each mode of transport. 
2. Vehicle: Mobile equipment unit, including tractive or propelling equipment, intended for transporting persens or goods. 
se Vehicle traffic: The movement of vehicles on networks. When a vehicle is being carried on another vehicle, only the movement of the carrying vehicle 
is taken into consideration. 
4. Transport: The carriage of persons or goods (including animals and vehicles carried on other vehicles) on networks as defined herein for each mode of 


transport, and not the movement of vehicles as such. It excludes the carriage of fuel and stores by the vehicle in which they are consumed. The weight of the 
goods is expressed in metric tons. 


RAILWAYS 


General 


в} Scope of the railway statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: These statistics refer to (a) all main-line 
railway networks, irrespective of gauge, and, where possible, to (b) secondary railways which carry out transport operations for the public. They exclude, 
however, networks the operations of which are wholly or mainly within one urban area. 


Networks 


6. Railway network of a country: The networks of all the railway administrations in the country. The network of a particular railway administration 
consists of all railway lines operated by the administration. It does not include stretches of road or inland waterway, even should rolling stock be conveyed over 
such routes, e.g. by wagon-carrying trailers or ferries. Main-line networks are distinguished from secondary networks. The most important network in any 
country is the main-line network; all other networks are regarded as secondary. ; 


Th Track; A pair of rails over which railway vehicles can run. 


8. Running track: A track providing end-to-end line continuity and used for working regular trains between stations or places indicated in tariffs as 
independent points of departure or arrival for the conveyance of passengers or goods. 


9. Line: One or more running tracks, each kilometre of line counting as one, however many tracks there may bel/. Where a section of network comprises 
two or more lines running alongside one another, there are as many lines as routes to which tracks are alloted exclusively. 


10. Lines operated for passenger transport: Lines operated normally for passenger and goods transport and lines normally operated exclusively for 
passenger transport. 


11. Lines operated for goods transport: Lines operated normally for passenger and goods transport and lines normally operated exclusively for goods 
transport. 

12. Electrified tracks: Tracks provided with an overhead trolley wire or with a conductor rail to permit electric traction. 

13. Electrified lines: Lines with one or more electrified main running tracks. Portions of line adjacent to stations that are electrified only to permit 


shunting and not electrified as far as the next station are to be counted as non-electrified lines. 
И RO ET 


1/. Secretariat note: The total length of line operated is the length operated for passenger or goods transport. 


— 153 - 


Vehicles 
14. Railway vehicle: Mobile equipment running exclusively on rails, moving either under its own power (locomotive and rail motor vehicles) or hauled by 
another vehicle (carriages, vans and wagon). 
15. Locomotive: Railway vehicle equipped with prime mover and motor or with motor only (electric locomotive) used for hauling railway vehicles. 


(a) Steam locomotives Locomotive, whether cylinder or turbine, in which the source of power is steam, irrespective of the type of fuel used. 


(b) Electric locomotive: Locomotive with one or more electric motors, deriving current from overhead wires or conductor rails or from 
accumulators carried on the locomotive. A locomotive so equipped which has also an engine (diesel or other) to supply current to the electric 
motor when it cannot be obtained from an overhead wire or from a conductor rail is classed as an electric locomotive. 


(с) Diesel locomotive: Locomotive the source of power of which is a diesel engine, irrespective of the type of transmission installed. However, 
diesel-electric locomotives equipped to derive power from an overhead wire or from a conductor rail are classed as electric locomotives. 


(9)  Special-system locomotive: Locomotive other than steam, electric or diesel, such as compressed air, gas or petrol locomotive. 


16. Rail motor vehicle: Motor vehicle constructed for the conveyance of passengers or goods by rail. In motor vehicle statistics, every indivisible set 
is counted as а rail motor vehicle; in statistics of passenger vehicles and of goods vehicles, each body is counted as a unit. The definitions of the various 
categories of locomotive: (electric, diesel, etc.) apply, mutatis-mutandis, to rail motor vehicles. 


ize Power of locomotives and rail-cars: Mechanical force developed by locomotives and rail motor vehicles, calculated in accordance with the formulae 
given in Annex | of document TRANS/WP.6/54/Rev.4. 


18. Passenger vehicles: Railway vehicle, which may be a rail motor vehicle or a hauled vehicle (passenger carriage), intended for the conveyance of 
passengers, even if it comprises one or more compartments or spaces specially reserved for luggage, parcels, mail, etc. These vehicles.include special vehicles 
such as sleeping-cars, saloons, dining-cars and ambulance cars, Each separate body of an indivisible set is counted as a passenger vehicle. 


19. Carrying capacity of passenger vehicles: The number of seats or berths available in the vehicle when performing the service for which it is primarily 
intended; in case of doubt, the capacity is the highest number of seats or berths available. Where accommodation is provided specially for standing passengers, 
the number of standing places offered is included in the carrying capacity, but must be shown separately in the statistics. 


20. Van: Railway vehicle, which may be a rail motor vehicle, forming part of a passenger or freight train and used by the train crew as well as, if need 
be, for the conveyance of luggage, parcels, bicycles, etc. Vehicles possessing one or more passenger compartments must not be counted as vans but as 
passenger-carrying vehicles. Mail vans, belonging to railway administrations, are included under vans when they do not possess a passenger compartment. 


21. Wagon: Railway vehicle, which may he a rail motor vehicle, normally intended for the transport of goods. 


(a) Covered wagon: Wagon characterized by its closed construction (solid sides all the way up and roof) and by the safety it provides for the 
goods conveyed in it (possibility of padlocking and sealing). 


(65)  High-sided wagon: Wagon with no roof and with rigid sides higher than 60 cm. 


(с) Flat wagon: Wagon without roof or sides, or wagon without roof but with sides not higher than 60 cm, or swing-bolster wagon. 


(d) Special wagons: 


(i) Insulated wagon: Covered wagon of which the body is built with insulating walls, doors, floor and roof, by which heat exchanges 
between the inside and outside of the body can be so limited that the over-all heat transfer factor (K or U factor) is equal to or 
less than 0.6 kilocalories (1 kcal = 4 185 joules) per square metre of the geometric mean of the inside and outside surface areas 
per hour and per degree centigrade of air temperature difference between the inside and outside of the body when empty, the 
values of the К factor being those obtaining when the mean temperature of the walls of the body is + 20°C (between +300C 
and +350C in the case of tank wagons for the conveyance of liquid foodstuffs). 


(ii) | Refrigerated wagon: Insulated wagon which, using a source of cold (natural ice, with or without the addition of salt; dry ice, with 
or without evaporation control: eutectic plates, etc.) other than a mechanical or “absorption” unit, is capable, with a mean outside 
temperature of +250 С, of lowering the temperature inside the body, when empty, to and thereafter keeping it for not less than 12 
hours at a maximum of +50 С with the aid of appropriate refrigerants and fittings. Refrigerated wagons must be provided with one or 
more compartments for the refrigerant which can be filled from the outside. 


(iii) | Mechanically refrigerated wagons: Insulated wagons, fitted with a refrigerating appliance (mechanical compressor, “absorption” unit, 


etc.) which is capable, with a mean outside temperature of +300 С, of lowering the temperature inside the body, when empty, to and 
thereafter maintaining steadily for not less than 12 hours any constant temperature level desired between +120 С and 00 C inclusive. 


(iv) Heated wagon: insulated wagon fitted with а heat-producing appliance which is capable of raising the temperature inside the body, 
when empty, to and thereafter maintaining it steadily at a practically constant value of not less than +120 С for not less than 12 hours 
when the average outside temperature of the body may fall to-100 С. 


(у) Tank wagon: Wagon fitted with one or more tanks specially designed for the transport of liquids or gases in bulk. 


(vi) | Wagon specially built or equipped to facilitate, reduce or eliminate handling of goods: Silo wagons, tip wagons, hopper wagons, etc. 


— 154 — 


(vii) Wagon specially built or equipped for the transport of: 
containers, 
or road-rail or road trailers. 


(viii) Other special wagons: All types of special wagon not mentioned above. 


22. Carrying capacity of wagon: The carrying capacity of a wagon is the maximum authorized weight of goods it can carry. 

23. Percentage of total park under or awaiting repair or maintenance: Percentage of vehicles temporarily withdrawn from service for maintenance or 
repair. Maintenance or repair comprises all operations necessary for keeping vehicles or putting them back in working order. 

24. New units placed in service during the year: Newly-built vehicles made available for operating for the first time during the year. 

25. Units scrapped during the year: Vehicles permanently withdrawn from service on the system during the year. 

26. Vehicles to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: The following vehicles 


must be included in the statistics of every railway administration: 
(а) all railway vehicles of the system, i.e. those actually at its disposal, including: 
(i) those under or awaiting repair, stabled or stored; 


(ii) those temporarily away from the administration’s network on “inter-system” working (locomotives, rail motor vehicles, passenger 
carriages and vans) or in the normal course of exchange between tailway systems (under RIV or similar arrangements) in 
connexion with inter-system goods transport; 


(b)  railway vehicles “Рог private use“, i.e. those which are neither owned by nor at the disposal of the system, but have their home station on, 
and are operated on, the administration’s network. 


27. Statistics of a railway system must exclude vehicles not at its disposal, for example: 


(a) any temporarily on its network in the course of inter-system working (locomotives, rail motor vehicles, passenger carriages and vans) or in 
the normal course of exchange between railway systems (under RIV or similar arrangements) in connexion with inter-system goods transport; 
or; 


(b) any which, although owned by the system, are on hire to, or otherwise at the disposal of, other systems. 


Staff 
28. Staff: All employees paid directly by the railway administration.2/. 
29. Total number of employees to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: Staff 


employed, in whatever capacity, during the statistical period in operating the railway, but excluding staff employed by ancillary services such as road 
transport, shipping services, hotels and restaurants2/. 


Vehicle traffic 
30. Train: One or more vehicles hauled by one or more locomotives or rail motor vehicles, or one separate rail motor vehicle running under a given 
number on distinct designation from an initial fixed point to a fixed terminal point. 
31. Passenger train: Train for the carriage of passengers composed of one or more passenger vehicles and, possibly, vans. 
32. Freight train: Train made up of one ог more wagons and, possibly, vans moving either empty or under load. 
33. Mixed trains: Trains composed of both passenger carriages and wagons and, possibly, vans. These trains should not be counted both as passenger 


and goods trains; apportionment of the kilometres run by such trains is made in accordance with the rules of the particular railway administration. 


34. Service train: Train of passenger carriages running empty, work train, repair train, breakdown train, trial train, ballast train, gravel train, 
snowplough train, etc. 


35. ; Passenger-train-kilometre or Freight-train-kilometre: Unit of measure representing the movement of a passenger or freight train over one kilometre. 
The distance taken is the length of line covered by the train on the railway administration's network. Shunting movements and journeys by train ferry are 
not included in train-kilometre statisti сз. 


36. Train-kilometres to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: Train-kilometres 
run by the various categories of train mentioned above, whether the vehicles are owned by the particular administration or by other systems. 


CL  ьнъЪУЪУУ У у, чун 


2/ Secretariat note: The results of a study now being carried out by UIC on staff statistics might necessitate amendments to this definition, together 
with changes in the employees to be included in the statistics (paragraph 29). 


- 155 - 


37. Wagon loaded: Unit of measure representing one wagon loaded with goods and despatched. Wagons loaded at private sidings, or harbour stations 
connected with a network and thereafter handed over to that network are considered to be loaded on that network. Wagons loaded on a secondary network 
connected with a main network and thereafter handed over to the main network are considered to be loaded on the main network, though the following 
are not regarded as being loaded on a particular network: 


(a) any wagon despatched with a load of goods transshipped from another wagon already loaded and despatched on the same network 
or 


(b) any wagon loaded during direct transshipment on rail of goods from a main network to another main network at a station with which both 
networks are connected (see the definitions of direct transshipment on railways in paragraph 55). 


38. Wagons loaded to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: All wagons loaded 

on the network. As regards secondary networks, only wagons not handed over to a main network should be included. 

39. Wagon entered loaded from abroad: Wagon entering loaded from a foreign network, in transit or far unloading in the country. 

40. Wagons entered loaded to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: All wagons 
entering the network loaded. 

41. Wagon-day: Unit of measure representing the presence of a wagon on a network for one day. 

42. Positive or negative balance of wagons exchanged with foreign railway systems: The difference during the statistical period between the number of 


wagon-days of wagons of the administration concerned on exchange on the lines of other networks and the number of wagon-days of wagons of other networks 
on exchange on the lines of the administration concerned, divided by the number of days in the period. This difference is positive if the first of these two 
figures is less than the second, and negative in the contrary case. 


43. Wagon-kilometre: Unit of measure representing the movement of one wagon, loaded or empty, over a distance of one kilometre, the distance being 
that actually run, shunting and other similar movements being disregarded. All wagon journeys over the lines of the network are included, irrespective of 
the ownership of the wagons. 


44. Empty wagon-kilometre: А wagon-kilometre run by a wagon without a load. 
45. Percentage empty to total wagon-kilometres: Empty wagon-kilometres expressed as a percentage of total wagon-kilometres. 
Transport 
46. Railway transport: Transport (as defined in paragraph 4) over the network (as defined in paragraph 6). 
47. Service transport: Transport which the railway administration performs in order to meet its internal requirements whether or not such transport 


produces revenue for book-keeping purposes. 


48. Transport for third parties: Transport which the railway administration performs for third parties, i.e. all transport other than service 
transport, including: 


(a) revenue-producing commercial transport (transport for hire or reward) and 


(b) transport free of charge. 


49. Passenger: Any person, excluding members of train crews, who makes a journey by railway vehicle on a given network, 
50. Passenger-kilometre: Unit of measure representing the carriage of one passenger by rail over a distance of one kilometre. 
51. Passenger transport data to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: The 


figures must cover all passengers carried by rail over the network of the administration concerned. Only transport by rail should be included: where a 
series of operations is carried out by different modes of transport, the figures should refer solely to journeys by rail. 


52. Every paying passenger must be counted; passengers carried free of charge must be omitted. It is essential that the data for passengers carried and 
passenger-kilometre data should be consistent with one another. Any passenger travelling successively over one or more secondary networks and a main-line 
network, or conversely, should be included only in the statistics of the main-line network. Any passenger using several secondary networks in turn should 
be counted only once. 


53. The distance to be taken into account is that over which the passenger actually travelled. 


54. Goods carried: Goods which have been moved by rail on the network of the administration concerned. The total quantity of goods carried опа 
network consists of the quantity loaded and of the quantity entered loaded (see paragraph 57). 


55. Direct transshipment on railways: Transshipment of goods from one rail vehicle to another where the distance between the vehicles is not such 
as to call for intermediary transport outside the station precincts. 


126 = 


56. Goods loaded: Goods placed on a rail vehicle and despatched by rail. Goods loaded at private sidings, or harbour stations connected with a 
network and thereafter handed over to that network are considered to be loaded on that network. Goods loaded on a secondary network physically 
connected to a main-line network and subsequently handed over to a main-line network are to be regarded as having been loaded on the main-line network. 
Not so, however, are goods which: 


(а) once loaded on a particular network, are transshiped from one rail vehicle to another on the same network; ог 


(b) on being handed over from one network to another, are directly transshipped on railways at a station adjoining another system (see 
definition of direct transshipment on railways in paragraph 55 above). 


57. Goods entered loaded: Goods loaded on a foreign network and having entered the network concerned by rail in transit or for unloading in 
the country; goods transshigped directly on railways on entering the network are also regarded as having entered loaded. 

58. Net ton-kilometre: Unit of measure for goods carried representing the carriage of one ton of goods by rail over a distance of one kilometre. 
59. Average haul per ton: Average distance each ton of goods has been carried on the administration’s network. 

60. Average wagon load: Average weight of goods per wagon loaded or wagon entered loaded. 

61. Goods transport data to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: The 


statistics should include all rail transport3/ performed on the network of the system concerned. Only rail-borne transport should be included; where 
transport is carried out successively by different modes of transport, the statistics must relate soley to the rail portion of the haul. 


62. The weight to be taken into consideration is the weight charged for in respect of revenue producing commercial transport, and the gross weight 
of the goods in respect of service transport and of free of charge transport for third parties. 


63. The distance to be taken into consideration is, 


(a) in the case of revenue producing commerical transport of goods: the distance charged for, with deduction of artificial surcharges for 
distance; 


(b) in the case of service transport and of transport free of charge for third parties; the actual operating distance. 


ROADS 


Networks, including Road Expenditure 


64. Network: The road network of a country is made up of all that country’s roads which are open to public traffic, including toll-roads. 
65. Road: Line of communication for the use of four-wheeled and other road motor vehicles running on their own wheels. 
66. Carriageway: Part of the road intended for the movement of road motor vehicles; the parts of the road which form a shoulder for the lower or upper 


layers of the road surface are not part of the roadway, nor are those parts of the road intended for the circulation of road vehicles which are not self-propelled 
or for the parking of vehicles even if, in case of danger, they may occasionally be used for the passage of motor vehicles. The width of a carriageway is 
measured perpendicularly to the axis of the road. 


67. Urban road: A road within the boundaries of a built-up area with a population of 5 000 or more. 
68. Main road: Road intended primarily for long-distance traffic or connecting principal centres of population. 
69. Motorway4/: Road, specially designed and built for motor traffic, which does not serve properties bordering on it, and which 


(а) is provided, except at special points or temporarily, with separate carriageways for the two directions of traffic, separated from each other either 
by a dividing strip not intended for traffic or, exceptionally, by other means; 


(b) does not cross at level with any road, railway or tramway track, or footpath; and 
(с) is specially sign-posted as a motorway. 


70. Roads to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: All urban and non-urban roads 
open to public traffic. In determining the length of roads, it is desirable that one and the same road surface should not be counted twice; and it is recommended 
therefore that, where possible, the method referred to in Annex 2 of document TRANS/WP.6/54/Rev.4 should be used, especially as regards urban roads. A 
note should appear in the statistical return saying whether or not statistics of urban and non-urban roads include double counting in respect of intersections. 


Vehicles 
TAY Road vehicle: A vehicle running on wheels and intended for use on public roads. 
72. Mechanically propelled road vehicles: Road vehicle, whether connected or not to electric conductors, fitted with an engine whence it derives its sole 


means of propulsion. These vehicles include trolleybuses and tramcars. 


oo 


3/ Secretariat note: Both transport for third parties and service transport should therefore be included. 
4/ As defined in the Convention on Road Traffic (Vienna, 1968), Chapter |, Article 1, (j). 


— 157 - 


73. Road motor vehicle.: Mechanically propelled road vehicle (including tractors) normally used for the carriage of persons or goods, other than 
vehicles running on rails or connected to electric conductors. Mopeds, as defined in paragraph 79, are not included among road motor vehicles. 


74. Passenger road vehicle 5/: A road vehicle designed, exclusively or primarily, to carry one or more persons. 

75. Passenger road motor vehicle 5/: A road motor vehicle designed, exclusively or primarily, to carry one or more persons. 

76. Goods road vehicle5/: Road vehicle designed, exclusively or primarily, to carry goods. 

JT: Goods road motor vehicle5/: Road motor vehicle designed, exclusively or primarily, to carry goods. 

78. Cycle: Two-wheeled or three-wheeled road vehicle, fitted with pedals and using human energy as its sole means of propulsion. 

79. Moped6/: Any two-wheeled or three-wheeled vehicle which is fitted with an internal combustion engine having a cylinder capacity not exceeding 


50 cc (3.05 cu.in) and a maximum design speed not exceeding 50 km (30 miles) per hour. 


80. Motor cycle: Two-wheeled road motor vehicle with or without a sidecar, not falling under the definition of a moped, and also a motor-driven 
wheelchair and a three-wheeled motor vehicle for the transport of passengers with an unladen weight not exceeding 400 kg. 


81. Private car: Road motor vehicle, other than a motor cycle, intended for the transport of passengers and seating not more than nine persons (including 
the driver). The term “private car” therefore covers taxis and hired vehicles, provided that they have fewer than ten seats. 


82. Motor coach ог bus: Passenger road motor vehicle, seating more than nine persons (including the driver). 
83. Number of seats in motor coaches or buses: Number of seats or berths, including the driver's, available in the vehicle when it is performing the 


service for which it is primarily intended; in case of doubt, the capacity is the highest number of seats or berths available. 


84. Total transport capacity of motor coaches and buses: Number of seats and special standing-room places provided for passengers8/. The number of 
standing-room places should be indicated separately in the statistics. 


85. Tractor: Road motor vehicle designed, exclusively or primarily, to haul other road vehicles. 
86. Trailer: Road vehicle designed to be drawn by a road motor vehicle. Trailers intended for coupling to agricultural tractors are not included. 
87. Semi-trailer: Trailer which has no front axle and which is coupled to the hauling vehicle in such a manner that part of the trailer rests on the tractor 


and that a substantial part of its weight and of the load that it may contain is borne by the tractor. 


88. Articulated vehicles: A unit made up of a road motor vehicle and of a semi-trailer. 

89. Combination of vehicles: A unit intended for the transport of goods, made up of a road motor vehicle and of one or more trailers (other than 
semi-trailers). 

90. Load capacity: Maximum weight of goods declared permissible by the competent authority of the country of registration of the vehicle. 

91. Permissible maximum weight: Total of the weight of the vehicle when stationary and ready for the road (including the weight of the driver and 


of all other persons carried at the same time) and of the weight of the load declared permissible by the competent authority of the country of registration 
of the vehicle. 


92. Goods road vehicles operated for hire or reward: Goods road vehicles operated, exclusively or primarily, in respect of transport for hire or 
reward (see definition of transport for hire or reward, paragraph 103 below). 


93. Goods road vehicles operated on own account: Goods road vehicles operated, exclusively or primarily, in respect of transport on own account 
(see definition of transport on own account, paragraph 104 below). 


94. Road vehicles to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: The statistics 
supplied should cover all the road vehicles listed in the relevant tables of the questionnaire (including those under or awaiting repair) and registered in the 
country and licensed to use roads open to public traffic, but excluding military vehicles. 


95. The number of vehicles to be shown in the statistics is that at a given date during the statistical period, the date being chosen so as to represent, 
if possible, the maximum number during that period. 


Vehicle traffic 


96. Vehicle-kilometre: Unit of measure representing the journey of a road vehicle, loaded or empty, over one kilometre of road, the distance being 
the actual length of road covered. Articulated vehicles and transport units made up of a tractor and trailer are counted as one vehicle. In all other cases, 


trailers are counted as separate vehicles. 


о SS ee 

5/  Vehicles designed for the transport of both passengers and goods should be classified either among the passenger road vehicles or among the goods 
road vehicles, depending on their primary purpose, as determined either by their technical characteristics or by their category for tax purposes. 

6/ As defined in the Convention on Road Traffic (Vienna, 1968), Chapter |, Article |, (т). For the purpose of this Bulletin, only the definition proper 
has been included, 

7/  Provisional definition pending the revision of Annex 9 to the 1949 (Geneva) Convention on Road Traffic. 

8/ This definition is of practical importance only for urban transport statistics. 


158 — 


97. Foreign vehicle: A vehicle bearing foreign registration plates. 
98. Vehicle-kilometres to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: 


(a) Internal traffic: The statistics should reflect the number of vehicle-kilometres performed on the territory of the country, regardless 
of the country of registration of the vehicle. 


(b) International traffic: The statistics should reflect the number of vehicle-kilometres performed in the course of international journeys, 
including frontalier traffic, on the territory of the country by 


(i) foreign vehicles, 
(ii) vehicles of the country. 


99. Entry of aroad vehicle: A road vehicle which entered the country, by road, loaded or empty. However, any road vehicle entering the country by 
another means of transport, the use of which for short journeys is dictated'by geographical or climatic conditions, is considered to have entered by road. 


100. Exit of a road vehicle: A road vehicle which left the country by road, loaded or empty. However, any road vehicle leaving the country by another 
means of transport, the use of which for short journeys is dictated by geographical or climatic conditions, is considered to have left by road. 


101. Transit of a goods road vehicle: A road vehicle which entered the country by road, loaded or empty, and which left it by road, loaded or empty, 
at a place different from the point of entry, provided that there has been no unloading or no loading in the country. 


102. Entries, exits and transits of road vehicles to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for 

Europe: The statistics should reflect the movements of foreign vehicles by road, including vehicles moving in frontalier traffic, across the frontiers of the country. 
In the case of buses, motor coaches and goods road vehicles, they should also reflect such movement of the vehicles of the country. Articulated vehicles and 
transport units made up of a tractor and a trailer are counted as one vehicle. In all other cases, trailers are counted as separate vehicles. 


Transport 
103. Transport for hire or reward: Transport for remuneration, of persons or goods, on behalf of third parties. 
104. Transport on own account: A transport operation performed Бу a person (physical or corporate). 


(a) — (1) either in his own vehicle(s); (ii) or in vehicle(s) placed exclusively at his disposal for internal transport, in compliance with conditions 
laid down in national laws and regulations when they authorize such placing of vehicles at disposal; or, for international transport, in 
compliance with conditions laid down in international agreements; 


(b) for his own needs9/ and for the transport (i) of himself, his family, friends or employees, ог (ii) of goods belonging to him, or (iii) of goods 
he does not own, but which he has bought, sold, borrowed or lent, loaned or hired, produced or processed, or repaired, always provided 
that transport constitutes only an ancillary operation. 


Passenger transport 


105. Passenger: A person is deemed to be a passenger every time that this person makes a journey on the network of the country in a road vehicle. 
Service staff assigned to buses, motor coaches, trolleybuses, tramcars and goods road vehicles are not counted as passengers. 


106. Passenger-kilometre: Unit of measure of the carriage of a passenger by road over a distance of one kilometre. 

107. Data on passenger transport to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: 

The statistics should refer to all passengers carried on the network of the country by the vehicles of the country and by foreign vehicles 107. The distance 
on which passenger-kilometres should be based is the actual distance travelled by the passenger. 

Goods transport 


108. Goods loaded: Goods placed on a road vehicle and despatched by road. When a journey is interrupted by a breakdown of the vehicle or for a 
similar cause and goods are transshipped from one road vehicle to another, this operation is not regarded as loading. 


109. Goods having entered the country by road other than in transit by road throughout: Goods which, having been loaded on a road vehicle in another 
country, entered the country by road and were unlaoded there (or transshipped to another means of transport). However, goods carried by a vehicle 

entering the country by another means of transport, the use of which for short journeys is dictated by geographical or climatic conditions, are considered 

as having entered by road. 


110. Goods having left the country by road other than in transit by road throughout: Goods which having been loaded (or transshipped from 
another means of transport) on a road vehicle in the country, left the country by road. However, goods carried by a vehicle leaving the country by another 


means of transport, the use of which for short journeys is dictated by geographical or climatic conditions, are considered as having left by road. 


111. Goods in transit by road throughout: Goods which entered the country by road and left the country by road 11/at a point different from 
the point of entry, after having been carried across the country solely by road. The considerations relating to short journeys by another means of transport, 
which were referred to in connexion with “goods having entered the country by road” and “goods having left the country by road” apply to goods in 
transit by road throughout. 


9/ “His own needs” includes the commercial and industrial needs of the undertakings concerned. 

10/ In the case of traffic for hire or reward, the exclusion of passengers travelling free of charge (e.g. small children) may be unavoidable. Moreover 
such exclusion might be desirable from the point of view of comparability with railway statistics. 

11/ Goods need not necessarily be carried in the same road vehicle throughout. 


— 159 — 


112. Goods carried: Goods moved by road on the network of the country concerned. The total quantity of goods carried in a country is made up of 
~ ool! of goods loaded in the country, the quantity of goods having entered the country by road and the quantity of goods in transit by road 
throughout. 


113. Net ton-kilometre: Unit of measure of goods transport which represents the carriage of one tom by road over a distance of one kilometre. 
114, Goods transport data to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: The 


statistics should include all road transport performed on the network of the country by the vehicles of the country and by foreign vehicles. 


115. : The weight to be taken into consideration is the gross weight of goods, including that of equipment such as containers and pallets containing 
goods, in respect of transport on own account, and the weight charged for, in respect of transport for hire or reward. 


116. с The distance to be taken into consideration is the actual distance covered in respect of transport оп own account, and the distance charged 
for — or failing that, the actual distance covered — in respect of transport for hire or reward. 


INLAND WATERWAYS 


Networks 


17. The network of inland waterways of a country is made up of all the inland waterways of that country which are open to public navigation (vehicle 
traffic) for the carriage of goods. 


118. Navigable inland waterway: A stretch of water, not part of the sea, over which craft of a carrying capacity of not less than 50 tons can 
navigate when normally loaded. This term covers both navigable rivers and lakes (natural watercourses, whether or not they have been improved for 
navigation purposes) and navigable canals (waterways constructed primarily for the purpose of navigation). The length of lakes is counted as that between 
the most distant points between which transport is performed. 


119. Waterways regularly used for transport: Waterways over which a minimum amount of transport is performed each year; this amount, expressed 
as ton-kilometres per kilometre of waterway, is determined by each government in the light of conditions prevailing on its waterway network. 


120. Inland waterways to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: The entire 
network of the country. 


Vehicles 
121. Inland water transport (IWT) craft: Craft having a minimum carrying capacity of 20 tons, designed for the carriage of goods Бу inland waterway. 
122. Dumb barge: IWT craft designed for being towed and not having its own means of mechnical propulsion. The fact that a dumb barge is fitted 
with an onde not change its nature. 
123. Dumb tanker: Dumb barge intended for the bulk transport of liquids or gases. Tankers for the transport in bulk of powdered products such 


as cement, flour, plaster, etc., are to be excluded, and to be counted as dumb barges. 


124, Self-propelied barge: IWT craft having its own means of mechanical propulsion. Dumb barges, pushed barges and pushed-towed barges with 
only an auxiliary engine should be regarded as dumb, pushed or pushed-towed barges as the case may be. -The fact that a self-propelled barge can be used 
for towing does not change its nature. 


124.a Self-propelled pusher barge: Self-propelled barge designed or fitted to push pushed or pushed-towed barges. 
125. Self-propelled tanker: Self-propelled barge intended for the bulk transport of liquids or gases. Tankers for the transport in bulk of powdered 


products such as cement, flour, plaster, etc., are to be excluded, and to be counted among self-propelled barges. 


125.a Self-propelled pusher tanker: Self-propelled pusher barge intended for the bulk transport of liquids or gases. Tankers for the transport in bulk of 
powdered products such as cement, flour, plaster, etc., are to be excluded, and to be counted among self-propelled pusher barges. 


125.b Self-propelled craft for river-sea navigation: Craft having a deadweight capacity of at least 20 tons, designed for the transport of goods by 
river and by sea and equipped with their own means of propulsion developing at least 50 hp. 


126. Tug: Powered craft developing not less than 50 hp and designed for the towing of dumb barges, pushed-towed barges, or rafts, but not for the 
carriage of Meng 


— 160 - 


127. Pusher craft: Powered craft developing not less than 50 hp and designed or fitted for the pushing or pushed-towed barges but not for the 
carriage of goods. 


127.a Pusher tug: Powered craft developing not less than 50 hp and designed or fitted for the towing of dumb barges, pushed-towed barges, or rafts, 
and for the pushing of pushed and pushed-towed barges, but not for the carriage of goods. 


128. Pushed barge: IWT craft designed for being pushed and not having its own means of mechanical propulsion. The fact that a pushed barge is 
fitted with an auxiliary engine does not change its nature. 


128.a Pushed-towed barge: IWT craft designed for being either pushed or towed and not having its own means of mechanical propulsion. The fact that 
pushed-towed barge is fitted with an auxiliary engine does not change its nature. 


129. Pushed tanker: Pushed barge intended for the bulk transport of liquids or gases. Tankers for the transport in bulk of powdered products such as 
cement, flour, plaster, etc., are to be extluded, and to be counted as pushed barges. 


129.a Pushed-towed tanker: Pushed-towed barge is intended for the bulk transport of liquids or gases. Tankers for the transport in bulk of powdered 
products such as cement, flour, plaster, etc., are to be excluded, and to be counted as pushed-towed barges. 


130. Carrying capacity (also referred to as “deadweight capacity"): Maximum permissible weight of goods, expressed in tons, which an IWT craft 
may carry according to the ship's documents. 


131. Power (hp): Mechanical force developed by the motive power installation in craft. This power (the unit of which is 75 kilogramme-metres per 
second) should be measured in effective horsepower (power transmitted to the propeller). 


132. Data on craft to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: The statistics should 


cover all craft, excluding harbour craft, seaport lighters and seaport tugs, craft able to navigate on rivers but which are authorized to navigate on the sea 
(coasters), listed in the questionnaire, including those under or awaiting repair, which are registered in the country or, if there is no registration of craft in the 
country, which are owned by persons (natural or legal) resident in the country. Figures in respect of craft in service should reflect the situation at the end of 
the year; those in respect of craft put into service during the year should refer to all craft placed in service in the country for the first time new or used. 


Transport 


133. Goods loaded: Goods placed in an IWT craft and despatched by inland waterway. Transshipment from and IWT craft to another craft does 
not constitute loading, nor does transshipment as a result of a breakdown or of lightening in the case of low water. 


134. Goods unloaded: Goods removed from an IWT craft after transport by inland waterway. Transshipment from an IWT craft to another craft 
does not constitute unlading, nor does transshipment as a result of a breakdown or of lightening in the case of low water. 


135: Goods having left the country by IWT (other than in transit by IWT throughout): Goods which, having been loaded on an IWT craft in the 
country, left the country by IWT. 


136. Goods having entered the country by IWT (other than in transit by IWT throughout): Goods which, having been loaded on an IWT craft in 
another country, entered the country by IWT and were unloaded there. 


137. Goods in transit by IWT throughout: Goods which entered the country on an IWT craft and also left it on ап IWT craft, at a point different 
from the point of entry, after being carried across the country solely by МТ. 


138. Goods carried: Goods which have been moved by an IWT craft on the network of the country concerned. The total quantity of goods carried 
in a country is made up of the quantity of goods loaded, the quantity of goods having entered the country Бу IWT and the quamtity of goods in transit by 
IWT throughout. 


139. Net ton-kilometre: Unit of measure of goods transport which represents the carriage of one ton by IWT over a distance of one kilometre. 

140. Goods transport data to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: The statistics 
should include all IWT transport performed on the network of the country concerned. 12/ 

141. The weight to be taken into consideration is the gross weight of goods, including that of equipment, such as containers and pallets, containing 
goods. 

142. The distance to be taken into consideration is the actual distance covered. 

12/. Secretariat note: The statistics of goods transport in any given country should relate not only to the tonnage carried under the national flag but 


to the total tonnage, irrespective of the flag under which carried. For the purpose of classification-of water-ways by economic importance, 
transport by raft should be included. 


— 161 - 


COMBINED TRANSPORT 


Equipment 


143. Container: An article of transport equipment (lift-van, movable or other similar structure); 


(a) of a permanent character and accordingly strong enough to be suitable for repeated use; 

(b)  specially designed to facilitate the carriage of goods, by one or more modes of transport, without intermediate reloading; 

(с)  fitted with devices permitting its ready handling, particularly its transfer from one mode of transport to another; 

(9) so designed as to be easy to fill and empty; and 

(e) having an internal volume of one cubic metre or more. The term “container” includes neither vehicle nor conventional packing. 


143.a Large container: A container, the capacity of which exceeds 3 cubic metres and with an external length, including any permanent attachment, of 
6 m (20 feet) or more). 


144, Medium container: A container, the capacity of which exceeds 3 cubic metres and with an external length, including any permanent attachment, 
of less than 6 m (20 feet). 


145. Small container: A container, the capacity of which is at least one cubic metre but not more than 3 cubic metres. 
146. Container fitted for special conveyance (‘à porteur aménagé’’): Large or medium container fitted with fixed wheels and which need, when being 


carried by rail, wagons fitted with special securing devices, 


147. Container for private use: Container which does not belong to a transport undertaking for hire or reward. 

148. Wagon-carrying trailer: Unit designed for the movement of wagons by road, otherwise than on rails. 

149. Road-rail trailers: Road trailer designed for the conveyance of goods and specially constructed or fitted to travel loaded on wagons. 

150. Data on combined transport equipment to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for 


Europe: The statistics should comprise all equipment (including equipment under or awaiting repair) owned or approved by the railway systems of the 


country. 


Transport 
151. _Number of containers forwarded: The number of containers loaded and despatched. 
152. Number of operations performed with wagon-carrying trailers: Number of journeys by wagon-carrying trailers conveying wagons loaded with 
goods. 
153. Combined transpogt data to be included in the statistics of the Inland Transport Committee of the Economic Commission for Europe: The 


statistics should include all operations carried out on the territory of the country and comprising at least a section of rail transport, with the equipment owned 
or approved by the railway systems of the country. The weight to be taken into consideration is the weight charged for in respect of transport for hire or reward 
and the gross weight of goods in all other cases; the distance to be taken into consideration is the distance charged for in respect of transport for hire or reward 
and the actual distance covered in all other cases. 


SEA PORTS 


Goods loaded and unloaded at sea ports: The figures for goods loaded and unloaded should represent the weight of goods (including packing) in external 
trade loaded onto and unloaded from sea-going vessels of all flags at the ports of the country in question. The goods should exclude: bunkers, ships’ stores, 
ballast, and transshipment (goods transshipped from an importing vessel to an exporting vessel). Goods unloaded into or loaded from bonded warehouse 


should be included. 


OIL PIPELINES 


Statistics on the network of, and transport by, oil pipelines refer to pipelines located on the territory of the reporting country, Excluded are 
pipelines of less than 50 km in length and all pipelines used for military purposes. International pipelines with a total length of 50 km or more should be 
included, even if part thereof, falling within one country, is less than 50 km.
